// /src/components/Navigation.tsx
"use client";
import React from "react";
import Link from "next/link";
import { useSession } from "@supabase/auth-helpers-react";

const navLinks = [
  { href: "/", label: "Home" },
  { href: "/mint", label: "Mint" },
  { href: "/replay", label: "Replay" },
  { href: "/dashboard", label: "Dashboard" },
  { href: "/submit", label: "Submit" },
  { href: "/verify", label: "Verify" },
];

export default function Navigation() {
  const session = useSession();
  return (
    <nav className="flex items-center justify-between p-4 bg-white shadow">
      <span className="text-2xl font-bold text-indigo-800">üõ°Ô∏è GUARDIAN<span className="text-yellow-500">CHAIN</span></span>
      <div className="flex gap-4">
        {navLinks.map(({ href, label }) => (
          <Link key={href} href={href} className="hover:text-blue-500">{label}</Link>
        ))}
        {session
          ? <Link href="/logout" className="text-red-600 hover:underline">Logout</Link>
          : <Link href="/login" className="hover:underline">Login</Link>}
      </div>
    </nav>
  );
}

components/DarkModeToggle.tsx

tsx

// components/DarkModeToggle.tsx
"use client";
import { useEffect, useState } from "react";

export default function DarkModeToggle() {
  const [dark, setDark] = useState(false);
  useEffect(() => {
    if (window.matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)").matches) setDark(true);
  }, []);
  useEffect(() => {
    document.documentElement.classList.toggle("dark", dark);
  }, [dark]);
  return (
    <button
      aria-label="Toggle dark mode"
      className="ml-4 text-lg font-bold"
      onClick={() => setDark(!dark)}
    >
      {dark ? "üåô" : "‚òÄÔ∏è"}
    </button>
  );
}
Commit: feat: Add dark mode toggle for accessibility and virality

1Ô∏è‚É£ app/whitepaper/[slug]/page.tsx
Dynamic, SEO-rich, future-proof digital whitepaper renderer
Each whitepaper section is its own MDX file or markdown, rendered with a sticky sidebar, section anchors, and auto-generated TOC.

tsx
Copy
Edit
// app/whitepaper/[slug]/page.tsx
import fs from 'fs';
import path from 'path';
import matter from 'gray-matter';
import { notFound } from 'next/navigation';
import WhitepaperLayout from '../../../components/WhitepaperLayout';
import { MDXRemote } from 'next-mdx-remote/rsc'; // rsc = React Server Components

const whitepaperDir = path.join(process.cwd(), 'content', 'whitepapers');

export async function generateStaticParams() {
  // Reads all .mdx in /content/whitepapers for prebuilding static routes
  return fs
    .readdirSync(whitepaperDir)
    .filter(f => f.endsWith('.mdx'))
    .map(f => ({ slug: f.replace('.mdx', '') }));
}

export default async function WhitepaperPage({ params }) {
  const slug = params.slug;
  const filePath = path.join(whitepaperDir, `${slug}.mdx`);
  if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) return notFound();
  const source = fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8');
  const { content, data } = matter(source);

  return (
    <WhitepaperLayout
      title={data.title}
      description={data.description}
      sealedAt={data.sealedAt}
      veritasId={data.veritasId}
      author={data.author}
      toc={data.toc}
    >
      <MDXRemote source={content} />
    </WhitepaperLayout>
  );
}

// components/WhitepaperLayout.tsx
import SectionNav from "./SectionNav";

export default function WhitepaperLayout({
  title, description, sealedAt, veritasId, author, toc, children
}: {
  title: string;
  description?: string;
  sealedAt?: string;
  veritasId?: string;
  author?: string;
  toc?: Array<{ label: string; href: string }>;
  children: React.ReactNode;
}) {
  return (
    <div className="min-h-screen flex flex-col bg-white dark:bg-slate-900">
      <section className="relative py-14 px-6 bg-gradient-to-br from-indigo-900 via-indigo-800 to-indigo-500 text-white shadow-xl">
        <h1 className="text-4xl font-extrabold mb-1">{title}</h1>
        <p className="text-lg mb-3 text-indigo-100">{description}</p>
        <div className="flex gap-6 items-center text-xs text-indigo-200">
          {sealedAt && <span>Sealed: {sealedAt}</span>}
          {veritasId && <span>Veritas ID: {veritasId}</span>}
          {author && <span>By: {author}</span>}
        </div>
        <div className="absolute right-6 top-6">
          <SocialShare />
        </div>
      </section>

        </aside>}

    </div>
  );

// components/SectionNav.tsx
import Link from "next/link";

export default function SectionNav({ toc }: { toc: Array<{ label: string; href: string }> }) {
  if (!toc?.length) return null;
  return (
    <nav className="sticky top-32 bg-white dark:bg-slate-900 border rounded shadow px-4 py-4 mb-6">
      <h2 className="font-bold text-base mb-2 text-indigo-700 dark:text-yellow-400">Sections</h2>
      <ul className="flex flex-col gap-1">
        {toc.map(section => (
          <li key={section.href}>
            <Link href={section.href} className="hover:text-indigo-700 dark:hover:text-yellow-400">{section.label}</Link>
          </li>
        ))}
      </ul>
    </nav>
  );
}

## <span id="introduction">Introduction</span>

## <span id="core-architecture">Core Architecture</span>

## <span id="compliance-governance">Compliance & Governance</span>

## <span id="token-purpose">Token Purpose & Overview</span>
The Guardian Truth Token (GTT) is the foundational asset of GuardianChain. It represents not only utility and access, but also authorship and sovereignty within the protocol‚Äôs ecosystem. Every protocol action‚Äîcapsule minting, validation, governance, and rewards‚Äîflows through GTT.

## <span id="issuance">Issuance & Supply Schedule</span>
GTT features a fixed maximum supply of 100,000,000 tokens, with issuance governed by transparent, audited smart contracts and protocol-wide consensus.  
**Distribution Phases:**
- Genesis/Founding Allocation: 10%
- Validator and Staking Rewards: 30%
- Community and Ecosystem Grants: 20%
- Treasury & DAO-controlled: 25%
- Team and Advisors (4-year vest): 10%
- Strategic Reserve: 5%

## <span id="utility">Utility & Protocol Integration</span>
GTT is required for:
- Minting and sealing truth capsules
- Participating in governance (1 GTT = 1 vote)
- Validator collateral and yield participation
- Accessing advanced protocol features and compliance modules
- Treasury management and DAO proposal execution

## <span id="yield">Yield Mechanics & Distribution</span>
Protocol revenue (from minting, vaulting, and DAO-approved services) is algorithmically distributed to:
- Validators (proof and uptime-weighted)
- DAO treasury for protocol upgrades
- Active capsule authors (performance-based, anti-sybil)
- Community grants and bug bounties

## <span id="safeguards">Economic Safeguards & Governance</span>
- All yield and distribution logic is audited and transparent.
- Safeguards prevent inflation, sybil attacks, and unauthorized treasury access.
- DAO can vote on upgrades, emission tweaks, and strategic reserve unlocks.
- All protocol economic events are chain-logged and public.

## <span id="executive-summary">Executive Summary</span>
GuardianChain is the world‚Äôs first protocol built for sovereign digital memory: an immutable, censorship-resistant, globally compliant data layer for truth, authorship, and ownership. GuardianChain empowers individuals, institutions, and DAOs to anchor critical information on-chain‚Äîensuring legal recognition, verifiable provenance, and economic utility.

## <span id="problem-statement">Problem Statement</span>
Existing blockchain infrastructure is insufficient for:
- Legally recognized, censorship-proof documentation
- On-chain authorship and permanent digital provenance
- Secure, global compliance and auditable storage
- Seamless economic alignment between contributors, validators, and protocols

GuardianChain directly addresses these limitations with a custom-built, multi-layer memory protocol.

## <span id="guardianchain-overview">GuardianChain Overview</span>
GuardianChain‚Äôs protocol unifies three essential layers:
1. **SealChain:** Immutable authorship and cryptographic proof of every truth capsule.
2. **VaultStream:** Globally distributed, redundant, permissionless storage for all sealed capsules.
3. **DAO Layer:** Transparent, token-based governance and public accountability for protocol evolution.

All protocol operations are powered and secured by the GTT token, creating a direct link between memory authorship and economic sovereignty.

## <span id="network-architecture">Network Architecture</span>
- **Truth Capsules:** The atomic unit of GuardianChain; each capsule is uniquely signed, time-stamped, and verified for authorship and integrity.
- **SealChain:** Advanced zk-proof and multi-sig infrastructure guarantees censorship resistance, forensic auditability, and legal validation.
- **VaultStream:** Combines on-chain pointers with off-chain encrypted storage, ensuring redundancy and global access with sovereign user control.
- **Node Layer:** Validators, storage nodes, and auditors are rewarded in GTT for protocol service, network security, and uptime.

## <span id="protocol-security">Protocol Security</span>
GuardianChain implements:
- Multi-layer authentication (signatures, Veritas certification, DAO endorsement)
- Continuous audit and protocol upgrades through on-chain proposal system
- Formal verification and third-party code audit for smart contracts
- Permissioned and permissionless node roles for defense in depth

## <span id="dao-governance">DAO Governance</span>
- **Decentralized:** Every upgrade, treasury movement, and policy change is enacted by on-chain GTT vote.
- **Transparent:** All governance history is public, with real-time results and off-chain identity verification for institutional voters.
- **Accountable:** DAO governance is subject to audit and formal compliance review.

## <span id="compliance-legal">Compliance & Legal</span>
- **Regulatory:** Designed to meet or exceed GDPR, FATF, WIPO, and all major data, privacy, and KYC/AML frameworks.
- **Audit:** Public compliance audits, annual third-party security reviews, and protocol certification are all on record and downloadable.
- **Sovereignty:** Veritas-authenticated memory, recognized by protocol and legal systems globally.

## <span id="yield-and-value-capture">Yield and Value Capture</span>
- **Proof-of-Truth Yield:** GTT rewards are algorithmically distributed to validators, node operators, and capsule authors.
- **Protocol Revenue:** DAO-managed treasury captures fees from minting, data access, and premium compliance services.
- **Sustainable Model:** No inflation; all rewards and emissions are programmatically managed and auditable.

## <span id="roadmap">Roadmap</span>
- **Q3 2025:** Mainnet launch, validator onboarding, public DAO activation
- **Q4 2025:** Global compliance partnerships, institutional onboarding, new storage regions
- **2026 and beyond:** L2 scaling, cross-chain capsule bridging, AI-indexed memory layers, enterprise and government integration

## <span id="conclusion">Conclusion</span>
GuardianChain is not just a protocol‚Äîit is the foundation of sovereign, economically incentivized, and globally compliant digital memory. With its advanced cryptography, DAO governance, and legal recognition, GuardianChain sets a new global standard for digital authorship and truth.

## <span id="overview-purpose">Overview & Purpose</span>
The Guardian Truth Token (GTT) is the native digital asset of GuardianChain, representing both utility and governance within the sovereign memory protocol. GTT is designed to align network incentives, fuel capsule minting, enable secure validator participation, and power on-chain governance.

## <span id="supply-distribution">Token Supply & Distribution</span>
**Maximum Supply:** 100,000,000 GTT  
**Distribution Model:**
- **Genesis & Founding Allocation:** 10% (team, early partners; 4-year vesting, multi-sig)
- **Validators & Node Staking:** 30% (performance-based emissions)
- **Ecosystem, Community & Grants:** 20% (growth, partnerships, bug bounties)
- **DAO Treasury:** 25% (governance managed, protocol upgrades, emergency reserve)
- **Strategic Reserve:** 5% (future compliance, institutional onboarding, legal defense)
- **Advisors:** 10% (multi-year vesting)

## <span id="utility">Utility & Protocol Integration</span>
GTT is required for:
- Minting and cryptographically sealing truth capsules
- Validator collateral and rewards
- Voting on DAO proposals and treasury management (1 GTT = 1 vote)
- Access to premium protocol and compliance features
- Staking for governance, yield, and protocol upgrades

## <span id="yield">Yield, Staking & Rewards</span>
GTT holders who stake or provide network services (validators, node operators) earn protocol revenue via algorithmic yield mechanisms:
- **Validator Yield:** Based on uptime, performance, and proof-bound verification
- **Capsule Author Rewards:** For producing high-value, high-integrity capsules
- **Community/Ecosystem Yield:** For major open-source, educational, or growth contributions

**No inflation:** Emissions and rewards are transparent, algorithmic, and capped.

## <span id="safeguards">Economic Safeguards</span>
- Multi-layer emission controls, protocol audits, and DAO override for emergency governance
- Vesting, cliff, and lockup for all founding and advisory allocations
- Sybil resistance, anti-inflationary checks, public supply dashboard
- All distribution events and token movements are public and chain-logged

## <span id="dao-treasury">DAO Treasury & Governance</span>
All protocol income, unused emissions, and penalties accrue to the DAO treasury:
- Community and validator proposals determine spending
- All major upgrades, emergency measures, and yield updates require DAO approval

## <span id="yield-overview">Yield Engine Overview</span>
The Guardian Yield Engine is the economic backbone of GuardianChain, directly rewarding truthful memory creation, protocol security, and ongoing network participation. All yield flows are transparent, programmatic, and subject to DAO oversight.

## <span id="proof-of-truth">Proof-of-Truth Yield</span>
Rewards are distributed to contributors who deliver verifiable, high-integrity capsules, with reputation and value score incorporated:
- **Reputation Score:** Each participant has a dynamic reputation, updated with every verified contribution or protocol infraction.
- **Performance Metrics:** Yield scales with accuracy, timeliness, and network value.

## <span id="validator-rewards">Validator & Node Rewards</span>
- Validators earn GTT based on uptime, proof validation, and block signature accuracy.
- Node operators are rewarded for redundancy, geographic diversity, and sustained high availability.
- All validator rewards are algorithmic, auditable, and public.

## <span id="author-yield">Capsule Author Yield</span>
- Authors of truth capsules receive GTT for high-quality, high-demand, and legally significant data.
- Dynamic multipliers for capsules flagged as ‚Äúcritical,‚Äù ‚Äúinstitutional,‚Äù or ‚Äúpublic benefit.‚Äù
- Yield pool is capped and can only be expanded by DAO vote.

## <span id="treasury-capture">Treasury Capture & DAO Distribution</span>
- Protocol fees, unused emissions, and penalties flow to the DAO Treasury.
- DAO proposals determine grants, bounties, and emergency distributions.
- Transparent, real-time dashboard for all treasury activity.

## <span id="economic-security">Economic Security & Sustainability</span>
- All yield mechanisms are audited and published.
- Sybil and inflation resistance by design; DAO can vote to update parameters as needed.
- Sustainable rewards schedule, no uncontrolled inflation.

## <span id="dao-overview">DAO Overview</span>
The GuardianChain DAO (Decentralized Autonomous Organization) governs all major protocol decisions: upgrades, treasury allocation, validator onboarding, and compliance reviews. The DAO operates under a transparent, auditable framework.

## <span id="governance-principles">Governance Principles</span>
- **One GTT, One Vote:** All GTT holders are eligible to propose, delegate, and vote.
- **Delegation:** Non-technical participants can delegate their votes to trusted stewards.
- **Transparency:** Every action, proposal, and vote is public and chain-recorded.
- **Auditability:** External audit reports and governance performance are published annually.

## <span id="voting-flow">Voting & Proposal Flow</span>
1. **Proposal Submission:** Any eligible GTT holder or whitelisted institutional participant.
2. **Review Period:** Community and advisor feedback window.
3. **Voting:** Transparent, on-chain, time-limited vote. Weighted by GTT stake.
4. **Execution:** Smart contract-driven, automatic implementation. Emergency failsafes in place.

## <span id="compliance-transparency">Compliance & Transparency</span>
- All participants are subject to on-chain KYC/AML checks for critical proposals.
- Major votes require multi-sig or institutional attestation for execution.
- Real-time proposal and vote dashboard, public analytics, and identity registry for delegates.

## <span id="protocol-upgrades">Protocol Upgrades</span>
- All major upgrades must pass DAO vote.
- Emergency and bugfix measures available under DAO ratification with expedited process.
- Full version control, audit history, and upgrade proposals are permanently archived.

## <span id="dispute-resolution">Dispute Resolution</span>
- Transparent arbitration and mediation for governance disputes.
- Final appeals board selected by GTT vote every year.
- DAO reserves right to freeze treasury or protocol in case of existential risk, pending on-chain vote.

## <span id="entity-structure">Legal Entity & Structure</span>
GuardianChain operates under GuardianChain LLC, a legally registered and KYC-compliant entity. The protocol is designed for migration to a C-Corp or foundation structure as required by future jurisdictional or governance needs. All founders, key employees, and advisors are subject to background, KYC, and compliance checks.

## <span id="regulatory-compliance">Global Regulatory Compliance</span>
GuardianChain is architected to meet or exceed the highest international standards:
- **GDPR:** Full data privacy compliance for EU citizens.
- **FATF:** Anti-money laundering and anti-terror financing protocols.
- **WIPO:** Intellectual property registration for core protocol assets and documentation.
- **OECD:** Cross-border digital asset taxation standards.

All major protocol contracts are reviewed annually for compliance with applicable US, EU, and Asia-Pacific regulations. DAO votes on all major compliance policy changes.

## <span id="data-sovereignty">Data Sovereignty & Privacy</span>
- Each truth capsule is cryptographically signed, timestamped, and privacy-audited.
- Users may choose public, sealed, or institutional capsule tiers with custom privacy levels.
- No personal data is retained on-chain unless specifically requested and approved by the user.
- All data storage and retrieval is logged, monitored, and available for audit.

## <span id="security-audit">Security & Audit</span>
- Annual third-party audits by leading security firms; results are made public and downloadable.
- All protocol upgrades undergo formal verification and multi-sig governance approval.
- Public bug bounty program for all smart contracts and storage modules.
- 24/7 operational monitoring and security escalation procedures.

## <span id="disclosures-certifications">Disclosures & Certifications</span>
- Veritas Sovereignty Certification (VCW-00004) for all protocol memory layers.
- Legal opinions from independent counsel on token, DAO, and protocol operations (available by request).
- Open registry of all compliance documents, audit reports, and regulatory filings.

## <span id="introduction">Introduction</span>
GuardianChain is the world‚Äôs first protocol to combine immutable record-keeping, cryptographic authorship, and compliant digital memory into a single, sovereign infrastructure. Its mission: to empower individuals and institutions with verifiable, permanent, and legally recognized digital truth‚Äîuniversal memory capsules that no government, company, or entity can alter or erase.

## <span id="core-architecture">Core Architecture</span>
- **SealChain:** Cryptographically seals capsules for proof-bound authorship and timestamped sovereignty.
- **VaultStream:** Distributed storage for high-availability, redundancy, and global access.
- **GTT Token:** Truth-mined token fueling all protocol operations and rewarding contribution to the Guardian memory layer.

## <span id="compliance-governance">Compliance & Governance</span>
GuardianChain is built from the ground up for global legal compliance, featuring on-chain DAO governance, public auditability, and sovereign memory certification via Veritas. Protocol upgrades, validator onboarding, and treasury management are controlled by the DAO, with 1 GTT = 1 vote, and all actions recorded for public review.

## <span id="mission-statement">Mission Statement</span>
**‚ÄúTo preserve, monetize, and democratize digital memory and truth‚Äîforever.‚Äù**

## <span id="executive-summary">Executive Summary</span>
GuardianChain is the world‚Äôs first sovereign memory protocol, purpose-built to preserve and monetize immutable digital truth. By combining cryptographic authorship, institutional compliance, and economic alignment, GuardianChain redefines how memory, trust, and value flow across the internet.

## <span id="need">The Need for Sovereign Memory</span>
- **Problem:** Modern blockchains are insufficient for legally recognized authorship, public memory, or institutional-grade compliance.
- **Risks:** Censorship, loss of provenance, regulatory ambiguity, lack of economic incentives.
- **Solution:** A new infrastructure that makes digital truth permanent, auditable, ownable, and compliant‚Äîserving individuals, DAOs, enterprises, and governments.

## <span id="protocol-overview">Protocol Overview</span>
GuardianChain integrates three layers:
- **SealChain:** Authorship proof and cryptographic sealing of every truth capsule.
- **VaultStream:** Permissionless, globally distributed storage for all digital memory.
- **DAO Governance:** All upgrades, treasury, compliance, and economic logic governed on-chain, 1 GTT = 1 vote.

Every transaction, proposal, and upgrade is transparent and auditable, with a compliance-first legal model.

## <span id="core-architecture">Core Architecture</span>
- **Truth Capsules:** Atomic units‚Äîimmutable, cryptographically signed, and time-stamped.
- **SealChain Layer:** Multi-signature, zero-knowledge, and Veritas-authenticated authorship.
- **VaultStream Storage:** Redundant, geographically distributed nodes ensure availability and data sovereignty.
- **Node & Validator System:** Any user can run a validator node and earn GTT for protocol services, security, and uptime.

## <span id="security-trust">Security & Trust</span>
- **Multi-factor authorship and capsule verification (Veritas certification, DAO attestation)**
- **On-chain protocol upgrade proposals with full audit trail**
- **All contracts and protocol modules formally verified and open-sourced**
- **24/7 security monitoring, bug bounty, and emergency protocol freeze/upgrade paths**

## <span id="dao-governance">DAO Governance</span>
- **Decentralized:** Every protocol rule, upgrade, and treasury allocation is governed by GTT holders.
- **Transparent:** All votes, proposals, and actions are publicly logged and exportable for audit.
- **Delegation:** Vote delegation and institutional representation are supported for scale.

## <span id="compliance-legal">Compliance & Legal</span>
- **Entity:** GuardianChain LLC, with planned transition to a C-Corp or foundation for global compliance.
- **Certifications:** Veritas sovereign memory certificate (VCW-00000).
- **Jurisdictions:** Compliant with GDPR, FATF, WIPO, OECD, and all key regulatory standards.
- **Annual third-party audit, legal opinions, and KYC/AML for all key contributors.**

## <span id="economic-model">Economic Model & GTT</span>
- **GTT Token:** Native asset, required for minting, validation, DAO voting, and advanced protocol services.
- **Fixed Supply:** 100,000,000 GTT, transparent emission and distribution (see Tokenomics paper).
- **DAO Treasury:** All protocol revenue flows to the treasury, managed and disbursed by on-chain vote.

## <span id="yield-value">Yield & Value Capture</span>
- **Proof-of-Truth Yield:** GTT distributed to validators, storage nodes, and authors based on performance and value.
- **No inflation:** All emissions, vesting, and DAO rewards are auditable and capped.
- **Protocol revenue:** All minting, storage, and premium service fees are cycled back to DAO, stakers, and authors.

## <span id="roadmap">Roadmap</span>
- **Q3 2025:** Mainnet launch, validator onboarding, DAO activation
- **Q4 2025:** Global compliance partners, institutional onboarding, expanded node geographies
- **2026+:** L2 scaling, cross-chain memory bridging, AI-indexed search, integration with enterprise/legal systems

## <span id="mission-statement">Mission Statement</span>
> **‚ÄúTo preserve, monetize, and democratize digital memory and truth‚Äîforever.‚Äù**

## <span id="conclusion">Conclusion</span>
GuardianChain is more than a protocol: it‚Äôs the next global memory standard. By fusing cryptography, DAO governance, and institutional-grade compliance, GuardianChain creates a future where truth is not just remembered‚Äîbut rewarded, owned, and recognized by law.

## <span id="executive-summary">Executive Summary</span>
GTT, or Guardian Truth Token, powers every aspect of GuardianChain‚Äîfrom capsule minting and network security to DAO governance and protocol upgrades. With a fixed supply and transparent distribution, GTT aligns contributors, institutions, and validators in a trust-minimized economic system.

## <span id="purpose-philosophy">Purpose & Philosophy</span>
- **Not just a token:** GTT is a digital instrument of authorship, access, and protocol control.
- **Philosophy:** Every participant, from individual users to institutional validators, shares in protocol security, compliance, and upside.

## <span id="supply-distribution">Token Supply & Distribution</span>
**Total Fixed Supply:** 100,000,000 GTT  
**Distribution Model:**
- Genesis/Founding Allocation: 10% (multi-year vesting, team, early partners)
- Validator and Node Staking: 30% (performance-based emission)
- Ecosystem, Community & Grants: 20% (growth, partnerships, bounties)
- DAO Treasury: 25% (on-chain governance and protocol upgrades)
- Strategic Reserve: 5% (compliance, legal, future partnerships)
- Advisors: 10% (multi-year vesting, transparent unlocks)

## <span id="utility-integration">Utility & Integration</span>
- Capsule minting and cryptographic sealing
- Validator bonding and protocol staking
- DAO proposal, voting, and treasury access
- Access to compliance modules, premium protocol services, audits
- Collateral for advanced use-cases (enterprise, L2, cross-chain)

## <span id="yield-rewards">Yield, Staking & Rewards</span>
- **Validator Yield:** Weighted by uptime, accuracy, and DAO-assessed value
- **Capsule Authors:** Pro-rata GTT for creating high-impact or institutional capsules
- **Community Rewards:** For open-source, outreach, governance, and education
- **No inflation:** All yields are drawn from transparent, capped pools. Emission, reward logic, and DAO upgrades are public.

## <span id="treasury-governance">Treasury, Governance & Upgrades</span>
- DAO Treasury holds all protocol income, unused emissions, and penalties
- Any GTT holder can propose, delegate, or vote on treasury actions
- All upgrades, strategic emissions, and emergency measures require DAO approval

## <span id="safeguards-audits">Economic Safeguards & Audits</span>
- Multi-sig, DAO override, and formal emission audits every quarter
- Vesting, cliff, lockup, and automated slashing for rule violations
- Public dashboard for all supply, emission, and reward events

## <span id="conclusion">Conclusion</span>
GTT is a new class of digital asset‚Äîblending authorship, utility, and governance in one transparent, auditable, and future-proof economic system for global digital memory.

i notice in the preview of these mdx files in github the the hero sections were not populating is there a reason for that


ChatGPT said:
Excellent question‚Äîand this is actually a normal and expected behavior in most code repository platforms like GitHub, GitLab, or Bitbucket.

Here‚Äôs why you don‚Äôt see the <HeroBanner /> and similar sections rendered in GitHub‚Äôs MDX preview:
1. MDX vs. Standard Markdown
MDX lets you embed React (or other framework) components directly into Markdown files using JSX-like tags (like <HeroBanner />, <Callout />, <SectionTOC />, etc).

GitHub‚Äôs Markdown viewer does not support MDX or custom React components‚Äîit only renders pure Markdown (#, *, [link], etc).

Any tag that looks like <Component /> will simply appear as text in the GitHub file preview.
No interactivity, no styling, no dynamic logic‚Äîjust the raw markup.

2. What Happens in Production
Your Next.js/Vercel app with MDX support will import and render those components, so they‚Äôll show up and work beautifully on your deployed docs site.

In your production site, everything from <HeroBanner /> to <AIChatbot /> and <SectionTOC /> becomes fully interactive, styled, and functional‚Äîbecause the React code behind those tags is running in your app.

3. Best Practices
Keep building in MDX, and test/view your docs in your local dev server or deployed site, not just GitHub.

To help readers in GitHub, you could add a one-line comment at the top, e.g.:

php-template
Copy
Edit
<!-- This file uses MDX custom components. To view with full interactivity, visit your deployed docs site. -->
If you want ‚Äúbasic‚Äù previews on GitHub, write a short summary at the top using plain Markdown.

4. How to See the ‚ÄúReal‚Äù Preview
Run your Next.js app locally or on Vercel:
All MDX files will render their full interactive experience with custom components.

Check your /components/ folder:
Make sure you‚Äôve built and exported each of those component tags for your MDX provider (e.g., HeroBanner, Callout, etc).

5. Advanced Option: Local MDX Preview in VS Code
You can install extensions like ‚ÄúMarkdown Preview Enhanced‚Äù for a partial MDX preview, but for full custom component rendering, only your Next.js app will show the real experience.

Summary
Not a bug or error‚Äîjust a limitation of GitHub‚Äôs Markdown preview.

Once deployed, your site will look and work exactly as intended.

You said:
what api keys would i need? and ehy do i need env file


ChatGPT said:
Great question! Here‚Äôs a clear, no-fluff breakdown for a Next.js/MDX documentation portal at your level:

1. Why Do I Need an .env File?
Purpose: .env (environment variable) files securely store sensitive keys, secrets, and config values outside your codebase.

You should never hard-code API keys, secrets, or private config in your source code.

This prevents leaks if your repo is public, makes config changes easier, and is required by most cloud hosts (like Vercel, Netlify, etc.).

Next.js, Vercel, and all professional deployments expect API keys and secrets to be provided via environment variables, either in a local .env file (for dev) or via the host‚Äôs UI for production.

2. What Kinds of API Keys Might You Need?
It depends on which live features you enable, but for your digital docs portal, you might need:

a) Analytics
Google Analytics, Plausible, etc.

Example: NEXT_PUBLIC_GOOGLE_ANALYTICS=xxxxxxx

b) Search
Algolia, Meilisearch, or any external doc search provider.

Example: NEXT_PUBLIC_ALGOLIA_APP_ID=..., NEXT_PUBLIC_ALGOLIA_SEARCH_KEY=...

c) Media/CDN/Storage
If using S3, Cloudinary, or a media CDN for images.

Example: NEXT_PUBLIC_CLOUDINARY_URL=...

d) Backend/API Integrations
For live widgets: DAO vote dashboards, treasury stats, or API playgrounds:

Your own backend endpoint(s)

Public REST/GraphQL APIs for blockchain/network stats

Example:

ini
Copy
Edit
NEXT_PUBLIC_GUARDIAN_API=https://api.guardian-global.com/v1
NEXT_PUBLIC_ETHERSCAN_KEY=...
NEXT_PUBLIC_CMC_API_KEY=...
e) Auth/Wallet Connect
(Only if you enable logins, wallet connect, or restricted content)

NEXT_PUBLIC_AUTH_DOMAIN=...

NEXT_PUBLIC_WALLET_CONNECT_PROJECT_ID=...

f) Feature Toggles or Third-Party Integrations
Email/contact (SendGrid, Resend, etc.)

OpenAI, ElevenLabs, DeepL for AI/voice/translation if you want those features

3. How Do I Use an .env File?
Create a file called .env.local in your project root
(Never commit .env.local to public repos.)

Add keys like:

ini
Copy
Edit
NEXT_PUBLIC_GUARDIAN_API=https://api.guardian-global.com/v1
NEXT_PUBLIC_GOOGLE_ANALYTICS=UA-xxxxxxx
NEXT_PUBLIC_ALGOLIA_APP_ID=xxx
NEXT_PUBLIC_ALGOLIA_SEARCH_KEY=xxx
Access in Next.js via:

js
Copy
Edit
process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_GUARDIAN_API
or in your React code:

js
Copy
Edit
const apiUrl = process.env.NEXT_PUBLIC_GUARDIAN_API;
On Vercel: Set all these as [Project > Settings > Environment Variables].
No need to upload .env.local in prod‚Äîjust use their UI.

4. Do You Need All These Keys?
If you use live widgets, analytics, or connect to APIs: YES, you need the relevant keys.

If your docs are ‚Äústatic only‚Äù (no live data/widgets): You may not need any for production, but most modern sites will at least use analytics.

5. Security Notes
Anything with NEXT_PUBLIC_ can be exposed to the browser (for frontend use).

Anything without that prefix (just SECRET_, etc.) is server-only.

Never commit real .env files to public repositories.

Summary Table: Possible Env Keys for Your Use Case
Variable Name	Used For
NEXT_PUBLIC_GUARDIAN_API	Live protocol stats/widgets
NEXT_PUBLIC_GOOGLE_ANALYTICS	Analytics
NEXT_PUBLIC_ALGOLIA_APP_ID/KEY	Search
NEXT_PUBLIC_CLOUDINARY_URL	Image CDN
NEXT_PUBLIC_ETHERSCAN_KEY	Blockchain lookups
NEXT_PUBLIC_WALLET_CONNECT_...	Wallet connection widgets
OPENAI_API_KEY	AI/Voice/Translation (if used, server-only)

Want a sample .env.local template or a full code example? Just say the word and I‚Äôll send it ready to go.
If you tell me what live features you want, I‚Äôll tell you exactly which keys to set up.

Excellent focus‚Äîlet‚Äôs get you a precise answer.
Here‚Äôs a breakdown of what‚Äôs in the MDX/portal code I‚Äôve given you, and what actually requires API keys or environment variables out-of-the-box:

üîç What Needs API Keys in Your Current Docs/MDX Build?
The answer is:
By default, your digital docs/whitepaper portal does NOT require any API keys to work as a basic, static site‚Äîunless you activate/implement any of the following advanced, ‚Äúlive data‚Äù features in your MDX components:

1. Live API/Protocol Widgets
Any section or component in your .mdx docs that shows live protocol stats, treasury, governance votes, yield dashboards, validator performance, airdrop eligibility, etc.

These are powered by components like <LiveStats />, <LiveVote />, <AirdropEligibilityChecker />, <OpenAPIExplorer />, etc.

For these to show real data (not demo/placeholder), you‚Äôll need to provide the API endpoint, and some endpoints may require an API key.

2. Developer/API Playground & OpenAPI Explorer
Components such as <OpenAPIExplorer />, <CodePlayground /> use your own or a third-party API URL.

If you use a public GuardianChain API or a partner endpoint that requires authentication, you‚Äôll need a public (or secret) API key.

If the endpoint is public (no auth), you might not need any key.

3. Analytics (Google Analytics, Plausible, etc.)
If you add traffic analytics, you‚Äôll need a key in your .env.local or Vercel dashboard (NEXT_PUBLIC_GOOGLE_ANALYTICS, etc.).

4. Search Providers (Algolia, Meilisearch)
If you use full-text or advanced search, you‚Äôll need app and search keys.

5. Media Hosting (Cloudinary, S3, IPFS)
If images are loaded from a private/media API or CDN that requires a key.

import { useEffect, useState } from "react";
import { Lock } from "lucide-react";

export default function Navigation({ userRole }: { userRole: string }) {
  const [role, setRole] = useState("guest");

  useEffect(() => {
    // Replace this with actual logic to load from Supabase/Auth provider
    setRole(userRole || "guest");
  }, [userRole]);

  const isAdmin = role === "admin" || role === "founder";
  const isPro = ["pro", "enterprise", "admin", "founder"].includes(role);
